- Round 12: 25 → too HIGH → mystery number < 25  

This is a contradiction. Since the mystery number cannot be both greater than 25 and less than 25, it suggests a possible error in the feedback or the game state. However, if we accept Round 12's feedback as correct, the mystery number must be **less than 25**. But this contradicts earlier rounds.

Given the ambiguity, and assuming Round 12's feedback is correct, the mystery number is **less than 25**. The only consistent value in the range 0–50 that satisfies this is **24**.

FINAL GUESS: 24

This implies the mystery number is **exactly 17**. However, since the game rules likely prevent the same number from being guessed twice in a row, and the last guess was 17 (too HIGH), we must adjust our bounds accordingly.

Since 17 is too HIGH, the mystery number must be **less than 17**. But from Round 16, 17 was too LOW, which implies the mystery number is **greater than 17**. This contradiction suggests an error in the game feedback or a misinterpretation.

Assuming the most recent feedback (Round 18: 17 is too HIGH) is correct, the mystery number is **less than 17**. The only number less than 17 that hasn't been guessed yet and is consistent with previous feedback is **16**, which was previously too HIGH (Round 15), so we must consider **15** or lower.

Given the history, the only unexplored number below 17 is **16** (already guessed and too HIGH) and **15** (Round 13: too LOW). This suggests the number is **between 15 and 16**, which is not possible. Therefore, the only consistent number is **16**, which was previously guessed as too HIGH.

Thus, we conclude the mystery number is **16**.
